GT(P,t)=0.2010739\cdot(-1+P/5.6366)\cdot(1-P/10.2326)\cdot P\;+\;0.2010739\,P\;+\;0.2010739\frac{P}{1+\exp(-5.6366(P-0.6341847))}.
\]

Key structural facts about GT:

1) **No \(t\)-dependence at all.** So any candidate must be made independent of \(t\) by setting all \(t\)-dependent coefficients to 0 (or otherwise making those terms constant 0).

2) As a function of \(P\), GT is **(cubic polynomial in \(P\)) + (logistic term in \(P\))**.  
The logistic term is exactly of the form
\[
K\cdot \frac{P}{1+\exp(-a(P-b))}
\]
with fixed nonzero \(K,a\).

So any matching candidate must be able to represent **a non-polynomial sigmoid-in-\(P\)** term of that specific type, in addition to a cubic polynomial.

Now check each candidate:

1. \(P^3,P^2,P\) polynomial + \(P*c5/(P+c6)\) rational + \(t\)-rational. Can kill \(t\)-term, but cannot turn \(P/(P+c6)\) into \(P/(1+\exp(\cdot))\). **No.**

2. Polynomial + \(P^2*c3/(P+c4)\) rational + \(t\)-rational + \(\exp(c9 t)\). Can kill \(t\)-terms, still only polynomial+rational in \(P\). **No.**

3. Polynomial + \(P*c4*Max(0,P+c5)\) piecewise polynomial. No logistic. **No.**

4. Polynomial + \(t\)-rational + \(\exp(c8 t)\log(Pc9+1)\). Kill \(t\)-terms ⇒ lose log term; remaining is polynomial only. No logistic. **No.**

5. Polynomial + \(P*c5\log(c6/(P+c7)+1)\) (log in \(P\)) + \(t\)-rational. Log cannot equal logistic for all \(P\). **No.**

6. Polynomial + \(P*c4/(P+c5)\) rational + \(\exp(c9 t)\). Kill \(t\)-exp, still rational not logistic. **No.**

7. Polynomial + \(c5\exp(c6/(c7+t))\) (only \(t\)). Kill it ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

8. Polynomial + \(\exp(c7/(c8+t))\) (only \(t\)). Kill ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

9. Polynomial + \(c4\exp(c5/(c6+t))\) (only \(t\)). Kill ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

10. Has \(P*c0/(P+c1)\) rational, and a power term \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) (monomial), plus \(t\)-rational and constant. No way to create \(P/(1+\exp(-a(P-b)))\). **No.**

11. Polynomial + \(\exp(c8 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

12. Polynomial + \(P*c4\log(P*c5+1)\) + \(t\)-rational. Log ≠ logistic. **No.**

13. Polynomial + \(P^{c4}c5\exp(c6 t)\) + \(\exp(c8 t)\). Kill \(t\)-exps ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

14. \(P^2\) + \(P\log(1+c2/P)\) + \(P\) + \(t\)-rational + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\). Even killing \(t\) and sine, remaining involves \(\log(1+c2/P)\), not logistic. **No.**

15. Polynomial + \(P*c3/(P+c4)\) rational + \(\exp(c8 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial+rational only. **No.**

16. Polynomial + \(P^{c4}c5\exp(c6 t)\) + \(t\)-rational + constant. Kill \(t\)-terms ⇒ polynomial+constant only. **No.**

17. \(P*c0 + P^{c1}c2 + \exp(c4 t)+c5 + \sin(\log(\cdot))\). Kill \(t\)-exp and sine ⇒ sum of monomials in \(P\) only. No logistic. **No.**

18. Polynomial + \(P^{c5}c6\exp(c7 t)+\exp(c9 t)\). Kill \(t\)-exps ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

19. Polynomial + \(P*c3/(P+c4)\) rational + \(t\)-rational + constant. Kill \(t\)-term ⇒ polynomial+rational+constant. No logistic. **No.**

20. Polynomial + \(P*c3/(P+c4)\) rational + \(\exp(c7 t)\)+constant. Kill exp ⇒ polynomial+rational+constant. No logistic. **No.**

21. \(P^2 + P + P^{c2}c3\log(Pc4+1) + t\)-rational. Log-power form cannot equal logistic. **No.**

22. Polynomial + constant + \(\exp(c9 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial+constant only. **No.**

23. Uses Max(0,·) and power terms plus \(\exp(c8 t)\)+constant. Kill \(t\)-exp ⇒ piecewise polynomial/power in \(P\), not logistic. **No.**

24. Similar to 21 but with \(t\exp(c6 t)\). Kill \(t\)-term ⇒ still log-power in \(P\), not logistic. **No.**

25. Has \(P*c1\exp(P*c2)\) (exponential in \(P\), but not logistic denominator form), plus constant and \(\exp(c6 t)\). Even with \(t\)-exp killed, \(P\exp(kP)\) cannot equal \(P/(1+\exp(-a(P-b)))\) for all \(P\). **No.**

26. Has \(\log(c7\exp(P*c8)+1)=\log(1+\exp(\alpha P+\beta))\) (softplus), not logistic fraction. **No.**

27. Polynomial but with \(P^2*c2\exp(c3 t)\) and \(t\)-rational. Kill \(t\)-dependence ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

28. Polynomial + \(\exp(c7 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

29. Polynomial + constant + \(\exp(c6/(c7+t))\) (only \(t\)). Kill \(t\)-exp ⇒ polynomial+constant only. **No.**

30. Polynomial + \(\exp(c7 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

31. Polynomial + \(\exp(c5 t)\) and \(\cos(c7\exp(c8 t))\). Kill those ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

32. Mix of \(P\log(1+c2/P)\), \(P\log(Pc5+1)\), polynomial, \(t\)-rational, constant. Logs cannot reproduce logistic fraction. **No.**

33. Polynomial + \(P*c5\exp(P*c6)\) + \(t\)-rational. Exponential-in-\(P\) term is not logistic fraction; cannot match for all \(P\). **No.**

34. Many terms with denominator \(c1+t\) and \(P*c7\exp(P*c8)\). Even if you try to remove \(t\)-dependence by setting coefficients to 0, you’re left with \(P\exp(P\cdot)\) at best, not logistic. **No.**

35. Polynomial + \(P*c4\exp(c5 t)\) + \(t\)-rational. Kill \(t\)-terms ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

36. Polynomial + \(c4\exp(c5 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

37. Polynomial + \(t\exp(c6 t)\). Kill ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

38. Polynomial + \(\exp(c9 t)\). Kill exp ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

39. \(P*c0\) + \(t\)-rational + \(\sin(P^{c4}c5+c6)\)+constant. Sine in \(P\) cannot equal logistic fraction for all \(P\). **No.**

40. \(P*c0\log(1+c1/P)\) + linear \(P\) + \(t\)-rational + constant + sine(log(P…)). Not logistic. **No.**

41. Same issue as 40 (with Abs). **No.**

42. Polynomial/power terms + \(t\exp(c8 t)\). Kill \(t\)-term ⇒ sum of powers in \(P\), not logistic. **No.**

43. Polynomial + \(t\exp(c5 t)\). Kill ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

44. All terms have denominator \(c1+t^2\). To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), you’d need all numerators zero except possibly if you could make the whole expression independent of \(t\), which isn’t possible without zeroing essentially everything; then you can’t match GT. **No.**

45. Polynomial + \(\exp(c7 t)\)+constant. Kill exp ⇒ polynomial+constant only. **No.**

46. Contains \(\sin(c5 t+c6)\) and complicated \(t\)-dependent denominators; cannot become \(t\)-independent while retaining GT’s \(P\)-logistic structure. **No.**

47. Polynomial + \(\exp(c5 t)\)+constant. Kill exp ⇒ polynomial+constant only. **No.**

48. \(P^2\) + \(P\) + \(t\)-only exp term + \(\log(c6\exp(P*c7)+1)\) (softplus). Softplus ≠ logistic fraction. **No.**

49. \(P^{c0}c1\) + \(t\)-only exp + softplus. Still no logistic fraction. **No.**

50. Polynomial with \(P^2*c2\exp(c3 t)\) + \(\exp(c8 t)\). Kill \(t\)-exps ⇒ polynomial only. **No.**

Conclusion: none of the candidates can produce the required **\(P/(1+\exp(-a(P-b)))\)** term while also being \(t\)-independent, except by zeroing it out—which would not match GT (since GT’s logistic term is nonzero).

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG13)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P + c6*P/(c7 + exp(-c8*(-c9 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand the first term:
(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) = -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/(5.637×10.233)

So the first part times 0.201*P gives:
0.201*P*[-1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/57.68]

= 0.201*(-P + P²/10.233 + P²/5.637 - P³/57.68)

= -0.201P + 0.201P²/10.233 + 0.201P²/5.637 - 0.201P³/57.68

Adding 0.201*P: the -0.201P and +0.201P cancel.

So the polynomial part is:
**0.201P²/10.233 + 0.201P²/5.637 - 0.201P³/57.68**

Which simplifies to: **c_a*P³ + c_b*P² + c_c*P²** (two P² terms can merge into one)

Actually: **aP³ + bP²** where a < 0 and b > 0.

The sigmoid part: 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))

This is a **logistic/sigmoid function multiplied by P**.

So GT = aP³ + bP² + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))

Key features of GT:
1. **No dependence on t** - GT is independent of t
2. Polynomial part: P³ and P² terms
3. Sigmoid part: P/(1 + exp(...)) - a sigmoidal function of P multiplied by P
4. No constant term (when P=0, GT=0)

For candidates with t-dependence, I can set coefficients of t-terms to 0. For candidates with exp(c*t) terms, I can set c=0 making exp(0)=1, turning it into a constant.

Now let me identify which candidates can match the structure: **aP³ + bP² + sigmoid_term_in_P**.

The sigmoid term 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P-0.634))) cannot be represented by:
- Simple rational functions P/(P+c)
- Logarithmic functions
- Power functions P^c
- Simple exponentials exp(P*c)

Let me check each candidate for the presence of a sigmoid-like term in P.

The sigmoid function is: P/(1 + exp(f(P))). This requires a term like `P*something` where `something` involves `1/(1+exp(...))` or equivalently `log(1+exp(...))`.

Looking through candidates, I need to find ones that have a logistic/sigmoid function of P.

Let me scan for candidates with `exp(P*...)` or `log(...exp(P...)...)`:

- **Candidate 26**: c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8) + 1) - This is a softplus! log(c7*exp(Pc8)+1). If c7=1, this is softplus(Pc8). The derivative of softplus is sigmoid, but softplus ≠ P*sigmoid.
- **Candidate 48**: c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1) - Same softplus structure
- **Candidate 49**: c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1) - Same

Note: log(c*exp(Px) + 1) when c=1 gives softplus(Px). But GT has P/(1+exp(-k(P-a))) = P*sigmoid(k(P-a)).

P*sigmoid is NOT the same as softplus. softplus(x) = log(1+exp(x)), and its derivative is sigmoid(x). They're related but not equal.

Actually, let me reconsider. Can any candidate reproduce P*sigmoid(P)?

None of the candidates contain an explicit sigmoid function of P (i.e., 1/(1+exp(f(P))) multiplied by P).

Candidates with P*exp(P*c) (like 25, 33): P*c1*exp(P*c2) is an exponential, not a sigmoid.

After careful analysis, **none of the candidates** contain the necessary sigmoid-in-P basis function that appears in the GT.

Let me verify each candidate verdict:

Candidate 1 through 50: All lack the P*sigmoid(P) term. The closest are softplus candidates (26, 48, 49), but softplus ≠ P*sigmoid.
